text:
I made this twice and both times it was gone in a day. I did change some things both time I made it 1. used 1/4 almond extract & 3/4 vanilla 2. added 1/2 tsp cinnamon & 1/4 tsp ground clove to the batter 3. made the streusel topping w/ 1/2 tsp cinnamon(from earlier reviewer).
One version was with walnuts, second was with sliced almonds. Both were good, not to sweet or tart, but the almond version was much better.

text:
This is the best cranberry dish I've ever made. I made it with a brown sugar/walnut topping (1/4 cup walnuts, 1/3 cup brown sugar, 2 tablespoons butter, 2 tablespoons flour mixed together), which definitely helped it, although it'd be good without the topping as well. I actually like it better cold than warm, but I generally like pies cold.

text:
PROS: A mix and dump pie that makes its own crust, nothing could be easier. Without exception, everyone liked it - even those picky eaters who wouldn't touch my homemade Cranberry Chutney - and some took home a piece for later.   CONS: The 1 tea. of almond extract would have been overpowering for my taste. I took the suggestion of another reviewer and used 1/4 tea. of almond extract and 3/4 tea. of vanilla. That was perfect with enough of an almond taste that other bakers could identify it in the pie.   SUGGESTION: After you pat the mixture in the pan, take a handful or so of cranberries and scatter them on top, pushing them gently about half way into the batter. Some will burst and run while cooking, giving the pie a more festive presentation with more red on top in lieu of a lot of the white batter showing on top.

text:
Oh wow!!  What a sweet surprise!!  This was SO GOOD!  It was yummy cranberry goodness surrounded by a tasty, tasty cake-thing.  I would describe the texture of the "cake" as a cross between a cake and a brownie (non-chocolate, of course).  I think the almond flavoring really ties it all together, and the nuts are essential too.  As I usually do, I used 1/2 cup whole wheat pastry flour in place of the white.  My husband was really blown away by this; he wasn't looking forward to "cranberry pie" but said it was one of the best things he's ever had!

text:
Outstanding exactly as written. You can reduce the berries to 1.5 cups if you're really not fond of tartness or if your berries aren't quite ripe. Leave everything else the same. I have always used frozen cranberries (not defrosted) and had no problems, but yes, the batter is very thick. It isn't a pie, but a sort of torte made in a pie dish. Don't do the cinnamon or strudel topping thing, it doesn't go with the almond flavor at all, and the almond flavor is the whole point of this dessert, which has the wonderful consistency of a (non-chocolate) brownie. If you like the flavor of marzipan then you will love this dessert. And honestly, can people stop giving negative reviews to recipes they did not even make? If you made this with blueberries and lemon extract and Egg Beaters, then you can't say the recipe is bad! You did not make the recipe!!!

text:
This was a great recipe - very easy and full of flavor. My husband and children loved it and asked me to make it again soon. The only change I made was to add 1 teaspoon of orange extract (because I was lazy and didn't feel like grating orange peel). It was the perfect blend of sweet and tart. I especially liked the fine sugar crust that formed on the top. To save time and use fewer dishes, I put the stick of butter in the pie plate to melt while the oven preheated. I took it out just before it had all melted and used a fork to rub the rest of the butter on the sides of the pie plate before pouring it into the mixing bowl. Thanks so much for a great recipe!

So simple and so delicious!! I followed the recipe exactly, except I used vanilla extract, instead of almond extract. . . Tis gone. Tomorrow I am going to bake it in my cast iron skillet. Pre-heat the skillet and melt 1/4 c. butter in the skillet before adding the dough (for it is more a dough than a batter, very thick, just spread it over your prepared pan). So, so good!! I'm sure the struessel is good, but as it this is a stellar recipe. Thanks!! UPDATE; Something I discovered by accident, if you first coat the cranberries in the sugar and then mix it all up, the sweet is right next to the tangy :) It also DID work in my skillet, only I used 1/3 c. in the batter and the remaining butter in the pan and I like it baked a little longer in the skillet for a true  cookie crunch! :)

text:
I love this!! It's excellent!! I did make several of the suggested changes.  I agree this is more like a coffeecake, the dough is similar to a cookie in thickness.  I added 1/2 t of cinnamon and the struesel topping that was suggested. I reduced the cranberrys from 2 to 1 1/2 cups, and rised them in warm water to bring them to room temp prior to mixing in. And I measured a little generously on the sugar to appeal to a wider audience.  I made an extra half recipe and made it in a springform pan, I probably could have fit a double batch in it.  Took a little longer than stated to get done, was less than firm when I took it out but it set up nicely.  It tasted like a thick cranberry walnut cookie bar.  I thought it was the best dessert there.  Everyone at work loved it and asked for the recipe!!

I made this for a work event, so I tripled the recipe. This comes out more like a cranberry cake, but it is moist and delicious.I tripled the recipe and I used one teaspoon of Almond, and two teaspoons of Vanilla-I think that was the perfect combination. In fact I have extra bag of cranberries, I might make one tonight! This one is a winner!

Deliciously tart and tangy.  I reduced the butter by half and the sugar a little and baked it in an 8x8 pan. It only needed  need 30 minutes in the convection oven. (Pie is a misnomer- it is a cake with no leavening!) I ended putting 2 Tbs of turbinado sugar on top for a crunchy finish.  It is perfect. I might add more almond extract and some dried cherries or try adding a few diced dates.

text:
Love this!  The slight sweetness of the cake batter, the tartness of the cranberries and the almond extract flavor make this dessert lovely and soooo good!  I made this several times last year and made it again yesterday for a potluck, everyone loved it and several asked for the recipe.  The only change I make is to use almonds instead of walnuts, but either way it doesn't make that much of a difference it is still delicious.  No other alterations for me I like it just like that.  The only thing I suggest is to not use frozen cranberries.  The recipe suggests you can use frozen cranberries but I tried that once and the outer rim got a tad burnt waiting for the middle to be done.  So make sure you thaw them if necessary.  Enjoy!

This had a winter holiday appeal with the red cranberries in the snow white cake.  I baked it in a 9 inch white ceramic tart pan instead of a pie plate and it looked beautiful.  This is not really a pie-like dessert and could use a better recipe name.  I did decide to stick with one type of nut, almonds: almond extract and sliced almonds (no walnuts) which worked well.  I used the topping idea from reviewer Nathan Bialke but used sliced almonds instead of walnuts: 1/2 c sliced almonds, 1/3 c brown sugar, 2 T soft butter, & 2 T flour.  The cranberries are a little tart in the sweet almond cake, but we liked it that way. I already have requests to make this again.

Never before rated a recipe on this site but feel I have to do so now.  DH and I absolutely loved this.  Used a bit of the sugar to sprinkle on the top but no other changes.  Have to stock up now on bags of cranberries. EDITED 9/13/15:  Have introduced this pie to many folks now and given out recipe so many times I can dictate from memory.  The only changes I ever make are sometimes swapping out almond with vanilla...I personally like the vanilla better, hubby likes almond.. and omitting the walnuts sometimes.  And I slightly reduce the amount of cranberries so that one bag makes two pies.  My picky s-i-l is planning on taking this pie to his family Thanksgiving and that is high praise from him. I make sure to buy several bags of cranberries before season is over so that I can store in freezer and then make this pie about once a month.  I prefer it cold. UPDATED 11/11/15:  For those who have problems using frozen cranberries... THAW before using them. Then you will have no problems.  My opinion of this dessert has not changed. Will be making for Thanksgiving again this year at request of family. I use one bag cranberries and double remaining ingredients to make two pies.  Then if not all eaten immediately I slice and freeze individual servings. Then doesn't take long to thaw one slice for me.  UPDATED 9/17:  My now 15 y-o gd requests this for every family get-together.  Have to make extra pie for her to take home.

I  rated this 5 stars really because it was so easy.  Everyone needs some quick and easy desserts in their recipe box and this one is added to mine.

I made two pies for two  potlucks and both parties raved about the pie. I made this on X-Mas Eve for X-mas the next day. I cut back on the cranberries (I used fresh) by about a half of a cup and used about half the amount of walnuts called for. I like tart things and this was really good. For me though, I think the whole 2 cups of cranberries would have been fine. One person I served it to thought it was pretty tart. However, everyone else who tried it (6 people) seemed to like it just the way it was. I sprinkled course sugar on top and it made it very pretty. I would agree that it is more cake like than pie like.. Whatever, I liked it. I know I will make this again. Good AND Simple, (and pretty too). Can't get much better than that!  Someone did mention that either adding blueberries or just making it with blueberries alone would be good too, I agree.

text:
I combined this recipe with the brown sugar topping of "Cranberry Upside Down Coffee Cake" so I made some modifications.  I reduced the amount of sugar in the batter to 3/4 cup and added the zest of one orange plus 2 tbsp orange juice.  I folded in only half the cranberries in the batter.  The remaining cranberries and walnuts I mixed in with the brown sugar and butter and poured in the bottom of a springform pan; I spooned the batter on top of this mixture and baked as instructed.  The results were a lovely mixture of sweet and sour and looked very pretty.

I've made this twice, and the first time I followed the recipe as written (except I used vanilla extract instead of almond). It had too many cranberries, and wasn't cooked all the way through. So I tweaked it a bit for the second batch and it was great! The second time I used only 1 c. cranberries, added 1/2 tsp cinnamon and 1/2 tsp ground cloves to the dry ingredients, plus sprinkled a generous amount of brown sugar on the top just before putting it in the oven. I cooked it about 7 minutes longer than the recipe called for, and it was just scrumptious! I brought the second batch to a Christmas party and it got rave reviews.

text:
Made this exactly as per the recipe (except I added fresh grated orange peel) and the cranberries were too tart for my family's taste.  Had most of it left over so tonight i will serve with a sweet orange glaze.  That might help.  The batter portion was nice and we loved the almond flavor, but sweetness was not enough to offset the tartness of the berries.  This recipe has potential, so next time, I am going to cook the cranberries in orange juice as I would for cranberry sauce, but just enough so that the berries have just popped and so that the sauce is very dry and thick.  Then I will combine it with the cake batter gently so that cranberries are just swirled into the batter.  This way the berries will have already been sweetened to cut the tartness, and it should work out better for my family's sweet tooth!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
A bit sticky and sweet for my taste (and I like sweet!), so I did a lot of experimenting, and here's my version. First, definitely have the cranberries at room temperature, it's so much easier.  Preheat oven to 350 F. Mix together: 1.5 cups flour, 3/4 cup sugar, 1/4 tsp salt, 1.5 tsp baking powder, 1/2 tsp baking soda, 1/2 cup ground almonds (or ground walnuts), and lots of grated orange rind. Go all around the middle of the orange; don't worry if it clumps in the flour. Once mixed, stir in 2 cups cranberries. Pour in 1/2 cup melted butter, 2 eggs (whisked briefly beforehand), 1 tsp vanilla, and optionally 1/2 tsp almond extract.  Stir carefully (but firmly) with a strong spoon.  Put it into a (greased?) 9-inch pan, and gently pat it down until flat.  I used a 9-inch silicon pan. The baking time is shorter! 32-35 minutes, definitely no more than 35.  Enjoy!

text:
This pie is a wonderful combination of sweet and tart flavors. I sometimes add pecans because my husband can't have walnuts but otherwise made the recipe exactly as written. It is so easy to prepare and has wonderful flavor. Thank you, Jean, for this delicious recipe!  Amendment: I have always made this with fresh cranberries and as such it is my all time favorite dessert. There are no fresh cranberries to be found at this time of year and so I tried frozen cranberries. I was really disappointed  in the taste of this dessert. It was way too tart. If you've only made this with frozen cranberries and didn't like it try again with fresh. It is wonderful with fresh cranberries. Adding some orange zest is great, too! I like to divide the batter into 3 - 6" pie plates and bake them for 28 minutes. One of the three pies is just the right size for my husband and I to eat with 2 slices each. I freeze the other two pies.

text:
I made this recipe by first melting the butter, then adding the sugar.  Next coat the cranberries with the sugar mix, that way each cranberry has its own sweetening.  I dumped in all the rest of the ingredients, put in 1/4 teaspoon almond extract, 1/2 teaspoon orange extract and 1/4 teaspoon vanilla extract and mixed it all thoroughly making sure that there was no flour on the bottom of the bowl.  I also added a handful of fresh blueberries and a chopped apple on the top of the pie and gently pushed it into the middle.  It is SUPER GOOD with vanilla ice cream when it is still warm.  This will be our new Thanksgiving Eve dessert!!

text:
I've made this recipe four times in the past two weeks using frozen cranberries from last season! It's been a big hit and friends have asked me to make it again and asked for the recipe. It's delicious and probably one of the easiest items I've ever baked. I made it three times in a standard pie pan and doubled the recipe to fit nicely in a 13x9 pan. The only thing I did different was to sprinkle a few extra cranberries on top as a previous reviewer suggested. Be careful with the almond extract, it's pretty strong stuff. I used only 1/2 tsp. in 9 inch pie pans and 1 tsp. in the 9x13 pan and the flavor blended perfectly with the cranberries. I will definitely add this to my holiday recipes. I'll also buy extra bags of cranberries before the season is over and freeze them so I can enjoy this at Easter and as a special treat throughout the year! Thanks so much for sharing this recipe!

I will need to rename this to quick cranberry bread. Very easy and delicious but really more like a cake or muffin. 2nd time I made it I used half brown and half white sugar. This is about the best dessert I've made from this site.  First off - it is most definitely more cake-like than a pie. text:
This was wonderful!!  I was concerned about it being way too tart, but it wasnt at all.  As other reviewers suggested, I used 1/4 t. of almond extract and 3/4 t. of vanilla.  I opted to use an 8 1/2" springform pan, rather than a 9 pie plate, which produced a pretty skinny pie, and even though I coated my pan generously with non-stick cooking spray my pie stuck terribly to the bottom of my pan.  Not the recipes fault, but next time I will use the pie plate or a smaller springform pan and I will put non-stick foil on the bottom for easier removal.  Regardless of my problems, this was delicious and Ill be making it again.  UPDATE 6/24/12 - I made this again using blueberries.  Very good!!

text:
Not bad. Mom liked that it wasn't too sweet. I followed the recipe exactly, except I opted for sliced almonds instead of walnuts, left out a tiny bit of sugar (1-2 tbsp probably), did 1/2 vanilla/almond extract, added a bit of cinnamon (1 tbsp?), and a tiny bit of clove and nutmeg. After baking it 35 minutes, I sprinkled on some Swedish chunky bits of sugar and baked it 5 more minutes. Then I left it in the turned-off oven for a few hours which might explain why the top crust was a bit crunchy. Next time, I'd halve or 3/4 the butter, pull it out of the oven on time and also try the streusel topping the other reviewers mentioned.

text:
I made a version of this pie gluten-free.  Since my family doesn't like cranberries.  I used apples instead.  I was skeptical when there wasn't any baking powder or baking soda, but only one reviewer mentioned adding a bit of baking powder, so I left it alone.  It looked like such a good model recipe that I changed it up to suit my family's tastebuds.
I used 1 cup of a gluten-free flour blend 
[the whole recipe is 6 cups white rice flour, 2 cups potato flour and 1 cup tapioca flour]
I did not have to add any xanthan gum for this pie to hold together.
2 cups of apples cut to the same size as the cranberries
1/2 cup granulated sugar
1/2 cup dark brown sugar instead of 1 cup white sugar, 
1/2 cup toasted rolled oats  
about 1/2 tsp cinnamon 
1 tsp vanilla (omitted the almond extract).  
I kept the eggs, salt, butter and walnuts the same.  Baked at the same temperature and for 45 minutes. Glad that I buttered every part of the pan that this pie touched.  The result was so good.  I want to try it  next with blueberries.     Thank you for such a delicious and easy recipe.
Laurie

Really good and easy!!! Didn't have a pie pan, just a glass pie dish, lowered the temp to 325 and also made the following changes:

Also added less then 1/8 tsp baking powder.

text:
This was unbelievably good, even though I changed the recipe significantly.  I live in a country where cranberries are not readily available, so instead, I used a frozen berry mix with cherries, strawberries, raspberries, and currants.  It was wonderful!  Nice sweetness, but the currants balanced it out nicely.  Like other reviewers- I added slivered almonds and a strudel topping.  The strudel topping was the one listed by another rater (1/3 c. br. sugar, 2 tbl butter and flour).  The strudel worked wonderfully- really made it work.  I would add it again every time.  I also made a change in using vanilla extract, as it was all I could find, but it worked nicely.  Added a little cinnamon to the batter too.  The pie needed baking for 10-15 minutes more than the recipe called for.  With vanilla ice cream this is a real treat!

text:
It's a pretty good recipe.  More like coffee cake than a pie.  Very stiff dough and does not rise much at all.  A bit too greasy for my taste, but my husband and my boss loved it.  Used 1/2 cup flour and 1/2 cup almond meal instead of 1 cup flour, and used vanilla extract instead of almond extract.  I also toasted walnuts before I added to the flour mixture.  The cake is pretty sweet, but I think it's a good balance with tart cranberries.  I baked it for 55 min, and it was still a bit gooey in the center.  Maybe because the batter has so much butter in it?  If I make it again (which I probably will), I will reduce the butter and add applesauce or buttermilk to keep it moist.

text:
As usual I didn't have all of the required ingredients so I improvised.
Instead of flour I used ground almonds.
I didn't have enough butter so added margarine.
And I only had one egg.
The mix was rather stodgy.
I couldn't find the base for my cake tin so I used a square 8-inch cookie tin.
Oh, and I only cooked them for 35 minutes because the oven is a bit dodgy and tends to burn cakes on top.
But the result was lovely.
I ended up with a batch of moist, nutty, cranberry cookies.
I'll be making them again though I'll definitely use only butter next time.
PS  For a nice chocolate torte or chocolate brownies use ground almonds instead of flour as the cake will have a richer flavour and be nicely moist.

Excellent and easy to convert to gluten free! I subbed with 1 cup Better Batter All Purpose Flour Mix.  My husband, who is not GF, enjoyed this dessert and said no one would ever know! Both of us enjoyed the combo of sweet and tartness with this recipe. Since I used chopped almonds (what I had on hand), I used 1/2 tsp Almond and 1/2 tsp Vanilla extract. text:
This is one of the best recipes I've found on this site. It is not a pie at all. The consistency is a bit like a torte, or a brownie. It's a bit chewy. Absolutely divine. If you like almond flavor, and especially marzipan, you will LOVE this in both flavor and consistency.

I am dumbstruck at people who rated this recipe and then said, "I didn't use the almond extract." OK, maybe it was good your way too, but it is NOT the same dessert AT ALL. The almond is what makes this dessert what it is. Don't sub it for vanilla. Just make the thing as is!

I used frozen cranberries and it went great. This is a really easy recipe. The batter is very thick, so just stir with a sturdy wooden spoon, and don't over-mix. Follow the directions and you will not go wrong.

country:
None
text:
This is one of my 'go to' recipes! I've made this for many years, and it gets raves. It's very good as written, but as we do with recipes we make for years, I have tweaked it.
I add a little more of the cranberries, and ALWAYS cut them in half. That way, the sugar and goodness gets in them.  I tried saving time  by putting them in the food processor and the flavor evened out to evenly sweet, it didn't have the pop-ups of tangy fruitiness. So I take the time to cut them in 1/2. 
Also, I up the almond extract to 3 teaspoons, yum!
Fresh or frozen cranberries, it doesn't matter. Frozen cranberries make the mixture very thick, but it comes out the same.  Also, I bake the pie  about  10 minutes more than called for, since the middle doesn't get done in my oven. Watch temperature, though, and don't overcook. The texture loses it's tenderness. It's always excellent served warm with a bit of vanilla ice cream!
One last tip, I often make two pies at once, and once cooled, tightly cover one and freeze it for the next event. I thaw it, warm it, and it's as good as fresh. When I make 2 pies, I add one extra egg to the mixture.

I'm updating my review: a year has passed, and this is by far the most requested dessert/ breakfast cake in our house. At the store today, one kid stocked up on bags of fresh cranberries so he'd be sure to have the ingredients on hand. Still following the recipe (though without the nuts, so the kids can take it to school.)
----------------------------------

We love this (though my 12 year olds will finish an entire recipe themselves if given the opportunity). I've made it twice (baked it once in a cast iron pan, once in glass; once with all purpose flour, once with whole wheat), and it disappeared both times within 15 minutes of coming out of the oven. 
With the frozen berries, I put half in the prepared pan, poured the filling over it, then pressed the other half of the berries into the top: no problems with the mixture getting too thick. I did sprinkle the top with coarse sugar (but that's the only real change I made.) Anything that my kids will eat with this level of enthusiasm is a winner!

text:
Made it the first time following the recipe exactly and it came out pretty good.  The second time I increased the walnuts to 1 cup and substituted vanilla instead of almond extract.  I then poured the batter into a CRUST made of 1 pack crushed grahams, 1/2 c chopped walnuts, 2 TB brown sugar, 1/2 tsp cinnamon and 1/4 c melted butter pressed into a spring form pan.  I also slightly undercooked the recipe so that the interior was more like a fudgy blondie than "a clean wooden pick".  After cooling, the pie sets up nicely and can be easily released from the pan.  Also, I use frozen cranberries for this recipe.  They stiffen up the raw batter quite a bit but the end result remains the same - awesome every time!

This was very good. I didn't use a pie pan because I only had a giant 10 inch deep dish thing and since I wasn't making a double recipe to fill it I just used a square baking pan (I think I used 8 inch) and it came out perfectly. I think maybe next time I may toss my frozen cranberries into my melted butter to defrost them slightly, or even let them thaw a bit on the counter before adding them, which may make combining the doughy batter a little easier. I also added maybe a heaping half cup of fresh blueberries in place of some of the cranberries and that was very tasty. I love this for when I'm craving that sweet almond extract flavour. My better half liked it too! Very much a brownie-ish texture... can't wait to make this again! I think combining canberries with another berry yielded the best results for me. I'll be stocking up on cranberries when the season hits so I can keep making this all year!

Ok folks, can you say "Tarty, nutty and simply delicious?" Than this unique dessert will not disappoint you. I make this wonderful dessert to compliment the Amish Breakfast Casserole (from this website) every holiday for my family and I always get smiles all around! I do tweak it a little bit by 1) sub roasted, crushed Almonds vs walnuts (which we prefer the taste) 2) dec almond extract to 3/4 tsp w/1/4 tsp vanilla extract and 3) made a brown sugar/almond strusel topping of: 1/4 cup crushed almonds, pinch of sea salt, 1/3 cup brown sugar, 2 tablespoons butter and 2 tablespoons flour mixed together. Again, it is a unique dessert that pairs up with a rich casserole/main dish. Oh, and don't forget the vanilla ice cream on top..delicious!

text:
I have been making this recipe for a few years now - it is always a hit! In fact, I buy a huge bag of cranberries and freeze in 2 c. bags so that I have fresh cranberries to use throughout the year.

There are a few changes I've made depending on the time of year. In summer, I use chopped, slivered blanched almonds and lemon extract in place of the nuts and almond extract. The tart lemon + cranberries make for a cool and refreshing treat with ice cream on the side. 
We also substitute pecans for the walnuts just because of preference - still delicious! 
Oh, it's perfect for breakfast, too. :) Enjoy!

text:
FANTASTIC (with revisions)
I made this pie with the revisions suggested (streusel topping w/cinnamon) and 1/4 tsp. almond extract + 3/4 tsp vanilla. The pie was a little gooey in the center after 40 minutes but still tasted good, the next day, it firmed up a bit and was moist with a texture that reminded me a little of marzipan (maybe the almond flavor helped that). The batter is extremely thick - like spreading cookie dough - but do not worry, it turns out amazing. My husband RAVED about it and my son who refused to eat it the first night (because he "hates cranberries") finally tried it and begged me to make it again since he had missed out on it. The neighbor inhaled some as well. I will be making this EVERY cranberry season. I have never had a pie quite like it and I LOVE it!! Try it with the revisions and you will not be sorry. I'm taking it to my next pot luck...

text:
Good, but tart.  I would definitely call this more of a coffee cake than pie.  I know some people baked this in a square pan which I think I would do if I baked this again.  It just doesn't seem right to have "cake" in a pie pan!  The cranberries I had were fairly large so that could have contributed to the tartness.  I did serve this with spray on whipped cream which helped.  I think it would be great with vanilla ice cream though I didn't have any.  I would suggest if you have larger cranberries that you cut them in half as some reviewers have.  If you don't have whipped cream or ice cream you may want to take others advice and add a streusel type topping.

text:
This is so easy and so tasty!  I didn't really know what to expect, but I didn't expect it to taste so good!  The first time I tried it, I didn't really care for the almond extract and I had pecans on hand, so that's what I used.  It was good.  But, I made it better.  The second time I made this, I used vanilla extract in place of the almond, used pecans again, and made a topping with more chopped pecans and brown sugar.  I baked it in a 9x9 casserole dish instead of the pie dish.  Perfection!  I was suprised at the nice balance of sweet and tart.  I had to bake another the very next day because my family devoured it in a matter of hours!

Wonderful recipe.  I used 1/4 tsp almond extract and 1 tsp orange extract, and always use toasted, chopped hazelnuts.  I have used a 9x9 Corningware dish, baked at 325 degrees for nine additional minutes, and doubled the recipe using a single layer 9x13 pan on 350 for about 45 minutes, turning the oven off and letting the cake continue to warm for additional 8 minutes before removing it from the oven to cool.  It was useful to spray the pans with a nonstick spray and dust with sugar.  Great with coffee in the morning, tea at four, whipped cream at midnight!

I also added some golden raisins that I had soaked in hot water for a short time.  The pie turned out great! Great dessert - with many options - it would work wonderfully at brunch with coffee and eggs! Yum!

text:
I make this dessert regularly.   My dad is a diabetic. I use Splenda baking blend instead of sugar (0 sugar in the blend) and I use 1/2 the butter and add a little unsweetened apple sauce as a substitute.  I use Truvia brown sugar topping.  It comes out tasting like a warm scone.  Bake it less if you like it soft, more if you like it a hard scone texture.  You can make this for breakfast to go with a nice meal or a dessert.  Serve with ice cream as a dessert or add whipped cream.  So good.  I also looked up a strudel type topping once and it came out great too.  There are other things you can probably do with it.  It's easy to experiment.

Oh my goodness, these were a hit! Cocktail party people couldn't stop eating them. They are sweetish (but not too sweet) and savory and those who love shortbread will love the almond flavor.  See below for recipe info, gluten free mod option and Add ons.

RECIPE: Followed it. Used frozen cranberries. They rock. Also used almond extract.

ADD ONS:
(1)White Choc Chips (1/3 cup of white chocolate chips (365 Brand, Whole Foods). 
(2)Topping: Blended 1/4 cup almonds, 1/3c brown sugar, 2T melted butter and sprinkled on. Also sprinkled on some demerara sugar for crunch. 

DIETARY RESTRICTIONS? If you are gluten free, they come out equally fabulously with King Arthur Cup for Cup GF flour.

text:
I got this recipe years ago from a friend in CO. We wait each year for the cranberries to come onto the island and then make the "pie " at least twice a month until the end of the season. I have made changes out of laziness. I use the whole bag of cranberries and pecan halves instead of walnuts. We prefer pecans and I usually have them laying around to make the candied pecans recipe found on this site. I may or may not snap the halves in half. Again, lazy. I also use a tablespoon of almond extract. We like cranberries and really enjoy the tartness of them. Because I use more cranberries than the recipe calls for, I have to cook it a bit longer. top it with custard and eat'em up!

Super easy!  I loved that I didn't even have to use an electric mixer - just mix with a wooden spoon.  To me, this is the perfect "coffee cake" to go with afternoon tea, morning coffee.   I love cranberries and was looking for something different to make with them. This filled the bill and I think it's a keeper!   I baked it in an 8x8 glass dish.  I love the look of the pie but I thought the square would be more practical for cutting small bites.   I used another poster's suggestion and used 1/2 tsp. almond extract, 1/2 tsp. vanilla extract, 1 tsp. orange juice and orange zest.  I loved the tart taste to this and it's a very pretty dish.  It was supposed to go to Thanksgiving tomorrow as an extra desert with my pumpkin cheesecake but I can tell it won't make it there.   DH and DS love it.   Already 1/3 gone!

I used whole wheat flour and my hand-picked currants, plus chia seeds for the walnut. It's rather good when it's hot, and probably heated up and a scoop of ice cream. But it is still a dump cake, due to the lack of leavening agent - so it  is a moist cakey dish. The chia surprisingly worked great.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Wonderful, unique, refreshing dessert!  Used the following:  12-oz fresh cranberries, divided (2 cups in the dough, remainder gently pressed into the top for a nice presentation); 1/2 cup sliced almonds for subtle taste and nice texture--have additional to press into the top; 1/4 tsp almond extract and 3/4 tsp Fiori di Sicilia extract  to enhance the citrus flavor of the pie; added zest of 1 orange (a must!); put all in a pie plate and topped with King Arthur Flour "Sparkling Sugar" for pretty presentation and additional texture.  Baked 60-90 minutes.  Good while warm, but fantastic the next day or day after!  This dessert will become a permanent part of my Fall rotation.

text:
I made no changes. In my oven it took an additional fifteen minutes to cook through and develop a brown crunchy top.
My concern: As an experienced baker, I adore using all the ingredients. Some of them are not exactly cheap. And fresh cranberries are seasonal.
So whereas I certainly recognize that an inexperienced baker could easily make this recipe... a good thing.....I would also observe that the end product is not remarkable in  any way and constitutes a terrible waste of gorgeous ingredients that might be more successfully utilized elsewhere.
Obviously a child, for example, might enjoy the effort. And God knows it's certainly edible, if forgettable....

This was really good! As per some of the other reviews, made a few adjustments, but I think the spirit of the cake was pretty much the same - and yes, this is more of a cake than a pie. I used almonds instead of walnuts in the batter, and didn't have almond extract so I used only vanilla. Love this recipe ... quick, easy, and delicious.  For my taste, I prefer using 1.5 cups of fresh cranberries (less tart than using the full 2 cups), 1/2 tsp almond extract, 1/2 tsp vanilla extract, and no nuts.  The batter is the consistency of soft cookie dough.  After baking for 40 minutes, the finished pie looks beautiful, and it tastes just as good as it looks.  I will be making this again next Fall when I can get fresh cranberries.

This is a crowd pleaser - I have a couple of variations.  It's good as printed or with gluten free flour.  I also make it with crushed pineapple/macadamia nuts/vanilla in place of the cranberries/almonds/almond extract.  My family likes that even better.  Reduce sugar to 1/2 c for the pineapple version. Only thing to watch for is that it does not brown like you'd expect.

text:
i made this following the recipe as written the first time and thought it was OK, but needed some changes.  Second time I doubled the batter and kept the cranberries to one bag; I used 1/2 cup almond flour (ground almond) plus 1 1/2 cups whole wheat pastry flour to give me 2 cups of flour and like I said I doubled the other ingredients except for cranberries.  I also used 1/2 tsp almond extract plus 1 1/2 vanilla because I knew the almond flour would give plenty of almond flavor (which I adore).  I added toasted slivered almonds instead of walnuts.  I used a ceramic deep dish pie plate and it was perfect for the amount of batter.  I topped the batter with washed raw sugar to give it a little bit of crunch.  I baked for about an hour but it could have used a bit more time; I think baking time is one of the hardest things to pin down, especially when I modify a recipe.  At the end of this process I had a beautiful cake/pastry that reminded me of the Danish holiday pastries a loved and devoured when I lived in Seattle.  The use of almond flour gives this cake a texture and flavor similar to marzipan.  The cranberries give it a bright burst of freshness that balances the sweetness.  It might not be everyone's idea of a success, but my family really loved it. o

This pie was a huge hit at a bible study of about twenty five people as well as a huge church event.  EVERYONE liked it and several people asked me for the recipe.  I did add the streusel topping from previous review adding 1/2 tsp.of ground cinnamon(also from a previous review) and sliced almonds instead of walnuts to streusel topping. First, I used blueberries instead of cranberries.  And, while it would have been better with Almond extract, I was out and used lemon extract instead.  Wouldn't recommend that.  This was nothing like a pie (unless you bake in a pie pan - then it's at least shaped like a slice of pie.)  It's a coffee cake.  Light?  Not mine.  I subbed Egg Beaters for the eggs and used the Splenda/sugar mix in place of all sugar.  Used pecans that had a sweet cinnamon glaze on them.  Chopped up smallish, but still didn't care for that texture in my coffee cake.  Kids wouldn't even give it a go.  I'll try a different coffee cake recipe next time (even though that's what it sounds like I did this time given all my substitutions:)  It was easy to make, however.  Sorry, Jean.
